<p>The <b>Belgian national football team</b> has officially represented <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> since <a href="/wiki/%C3%89vence_Copp%C3%A9e_Trophy" title="Évence Coppée Trophy">their maiden match</a> in 1904. The squad is under the global jurisdiction of <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> and is governed in Europe by <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>—both of which were co-founded by the Belgian team's supervising body, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Belgian_Football_Association" title="Royal Belgian Football Association">Royal Belgian Football Association</a> (RBFA). Periods of regular Belgian representation at the highest international level, from 1920 to 1938, and 1970 to 2002, have alternated with mostly unsuccessful qualification rounds. Most of Belgium's home games are played at the <a href="/wiki/King_Baudouin_Stadium" title="King Baudouin Stadium">King Baudouin Stadium</a> in Brussels.</p>
<p>Belgium's national team has participated in three quadrennial major football competitions. It appeared in the end stages of twelve <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a> and five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Football_Championship" title="UEFA European Football Championship">UEFA European Football Championships</a>, and featured at three Olympic football tournaments, including the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1920_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1920 Summer Olympics">1920 Olympic tournament</a> which they won. Other notable performances are victories over four <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup#Results" title="FIFA World Cup">reigning world champions</a>—West Germany, Brazil, Argentina and France—between 1954 and 2002. Belgium has long-standing football rivalries with its Dutch and French counterparts, having played both teams nearly every year from 1905 to 1967. The squad has been known as the Red Devils since 1906; its fan club is named "1895".</p>
<p>During the national player career of forward <a href="/wiki/Paul_Van_Himst" title="Paul Van Himst">Paul Van Himst</a>, the most-praised Belgian footballer of the 20th century, Belgium took third place at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_1972" title="Euro 1972">Euro 1972</a>. After that, they experienced two <a href="/wiki/Golden_generation" title="Golden generation">golden ages</a> with many gifted players. In the first period, which lasted from the 1980s to the early 1990s, the team finished as runners-up at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_1980" title="Euro 1980">Euro 1980</a> and fourth in the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 World Cup</a>. In the second, under guidance of <a href="/wiki/Marc_Wilmots" title="Marc Wilmots">Marc Wilmots</a> in the 2010s, Belgium topped the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a> for the first time in November 2015. Between September 2016 and October 2017, they are competing in the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">European qualifiers for the 2018 World Cup</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Belgium_national_football_team" title="History of the Belgium national football team">History of the Belgium national football team</a></div>
<p>Belgium was one of the first mainland European countries to play association football.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[6]</a></sup> Its practice in Belgium began on 26 October 1863, after an Irish student walked into the Josephites College of <a href="/wiki/Melle,_Belgium" title="Melle, Belgium">Melle</a> with a leather ball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[7]</a></sup> Initially an elitist pastime,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup> during the following decades association football supplanted <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a> as Belgium's most popular football sport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197975_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197975-11">[9]</a></sup> On 1 September 1895, ten clubs for football, athletics, cricket and cycling founded the Belgian sports board Union Belge des Sociétés de Sports Athlétiques (UBSSA);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197975_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197975-11">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RBFAhistFr_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-RBFAhistFr-12">[10]</a></sup> a year later UBSSA organised <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgian_First_Division_1895-96" title="Belgian First Division 1895-96">the first annual league in Belgian football</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197975_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197975-11">[9]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BelgiumNFT1901.jpg"><img alt="Football team in uniform" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="390" data-file-width="701" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/BelgiumNFT1901.jpg/260px-BelgiumNFT1901.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/BelgiumNFT1901.jpg/390px-BelgiumNFT1901.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/BelgiumNFT1901.jpg/520px-BelgiumNFT1901.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BelgiumNFT1901.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The first Belgium A-squad in 1901 featured four Englishmen.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 11 October 1900, <a href="/wiki/K._Beerschot_V.A.C." title="K. Beerschot V.A.C.">Beerschot AC</a> honorary president Jorge Díaz announced that <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> would host a series of challenge matches between Europe's best football teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuldemontDeps199564_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuldemontDeps199564-13">[11]</a></sup> After some organisational problems, on 28 April 1901, Beerschot's pitch hosted its first tournament, in which a Belgian A-squad and a Dutch B-team contested the Coupe Vanden Abeele.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraipontsWillocx2003_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraipontsWillocx2003-14">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TrouwCVA_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-TrouwCVA-15">[13]</a></sup> Belgium won,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHubert198012_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHubert198012-16">[14]</a></sup> and beat the Netherlands in all three follow-up games;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHubert198013_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHubert198013-17">[15]</a></sup> FIFA does not recognise these results because Belgium fielded some English players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHubert198013_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHubert198013-17">[15]</a></sup> On 1 May 1904, the Belgians played their first official game, against <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Stade_du_Vivier_d%27Oie" title="Stade du Vivier d'Oie">Stade du Vivier d'Oie</a> in Uccle; their draw left the Évence Coppée Trophy unclaimed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UEFABelFra1904_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-UEFABelFra1904-18">[16]</a></sup> Twenty days later, the <a href="/wiki/Football_association" title="Football association">football boards</a> of both countries were among the seven FIFA founders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParrishNauright2014xv_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParrishNauright2014xv-20">[18]</a></sup> At that time, the Belgian squad was chosen by a committee drawn from the country's six or seven major clubs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoin1945_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoin1945-21">[19]</a></sup> In 1906, the national team players received the nickname Red Devils because of their red jerseys,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuldemontDeps199565_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuldemontDeps199565-22">[20]</a></sup> and four years later, Scottish ex-footballer <a href="/wiki/William_Maxwell_(footballer)" title="William Maxwell (footballer)">William Maxwell</a> replaced the UBSSA committee as their manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manrsssf_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-manrsssf-23">[21]</a></sup> From 1912, UBSSA governed football only and was renamed UBSFA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[C]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RBFAhist_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-RBFAhist-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197975_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197975-11">[9]</a></sup> During the Great War, the national team only played <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team_results_%E2%80%93_unofficial_matches" title="Belgium national football team results – unofficial matches">unrecognised friendlies</a>, with games in and against France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DT210316_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-DT210316-26">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/1920_Summer_Olympics" title="1920 Summer Olympics">1920 Summer Olympics</a>, in their first official Olympic appearance, the Red Devils won the gold medal on home soil after <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1920_Summer_Olympics#Gold_medal_match" title="Football at the 1920 Summer Olympics">a controversial final</a> in which their Czechoslovak opponents left the pitch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISOH_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-ISOH-27">[24]</a></sup> This triumph led them to an all-time high second place in the <a href="/wiki/World_Football_Elo_Ratings" title="World Football Elo Ratings">World Football Elo Ratings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elo180813_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-Elo180813-5">[4]</a></sup> In the three 1920s Summer Olympics, they achieved fair results (four wins in seven games), and played their first intercontinental match, against <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup> Over the following decade, however, Belgium lost all of their matches at the first three FIFA World Cup final tournaments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup> According to historian Richard Henshaw, "The growth of [football] in Scandinavia, Central Europe, and South America left Belgium far behind".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197976_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197976-28">[25]</a></sup> Although World War II hindered international football events in the 1940s, the Belgian team remained active with unofficial matches against squads of other <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">allied nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[26]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1920_Olympic_football_final_(Belgium_v._Czechoslovakia),_penalty_Copp%C3%A9e.jpg"><img alt="A successful penalty kick, seen from the back of the net" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="276" data-file-width="460" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/1920_Olympic_football_final_%28Belgium_v._Czechoslovakia%29%2C_penalty_Copp%C3%A9e.jpg/260px-1920_Olympic_football_final_%28Belgium_v._Czechoslovakia%29%2C_penalty_Copp%C3%A9e.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/1920_Olympic_football_final_%28Belgium_v._Czechoslovakia%29%2C_penalty_Copp%C3%A9e.jpg/390px-1920_Olympic_football_final_%28Belgium_v._Czechoslovakia%29%2C_penalty_Copp%C3%A9e.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9e/1920_Olympic_football_final_%28Belgium_v._Czechoslovakia%29%2C_penalty_Copp%C3%A9e.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1920_Olympic_football_final_(Belgium_v._Czechoslovakia),_penalty_Copp%C3%A9e.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
In the 1920 Olympic football final at the <a href="/wiki/Olympisch_Stadion_(Antwerp)" title="Olympisch Stadion (Antwerp)">Olympisch Stadion</a> in Antwerp, Robert Coppée scored for Belgium with a penalty kick.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Belgium qualified for only one of eight major tournaments during the 1950s and the 1960s: the <a href="/wiki/1954_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1954 FIFA World Cup">1954 World Cup</a>. The day before the tournament began, the RBFA was among the three UEFA founders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[27]</a></sup> Dutch journalists considered the draw of the 1954 Belgian team in their opener against <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> to be the most surprising result of that match day, even more than <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a>'s victory over the Italian "football stars".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AD180654_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-AD180654-31">[28]</a></sup> However, Belgium were eliminated after a loss to <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> in the second (and last) group match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf54_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf54-32">[29]</a></sup> Two bright spots in these decades were wins against World Cup holders: <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">West Germany</a> in 1954, and <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a> in 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup> Between these, Belgium defeated Hungary's <a href="/wiki/Golden_Team" title="Golden Team">Golden Team</a> in 1956.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-4"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup> The combination of failure in competitive games, and success in exhibition matches, gave the Belgians the mock title of "world champion of the friendlies".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBernhartHoutman2014_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBernhartHoutman2014-34">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>The team's performance improved during the early 1970s, under manager <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Goethals" title="Raymond Goethals">Raymond Goethals</a>. Fully dressed in white, as the White Devils,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WhiteDevil_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-WhiteDevil-35">[32]</a></sup> Belgium had their first victories at World and European Championships at the <a href="/wiki/1970_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1970 FIFA World Cup">1970 World Cup</a> and Euro 1972.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf70_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf70-36">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf72_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf72-37">[34]</a></sup> En route to that Euro appearance, their first, they eliminated <a href="/wiki/List_of_UEFA_European_Championship_records#General_statistics_by_tournament" title="List of UEFA European Championship records">reigning European champions</a> Italy by winning <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1972_qualifying_play-offs" title="UEFA Euro 1972 qualifying play-offs">the two-legged play-offs</a> on <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_association_football_terms#A" title="Glossary of association football terms">aggregate</a>. At the end stage, they finished third by winning the consolation match against Hungary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf72_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf72-37">[34]</a></sup> In 1973, the denial of a match-winning goal in their last <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="1974 FIFA World Cup qualification">1974 FIFA World Cup qualification</a> game for UEFA Group 3 cost Belgium their appearance at the finals,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup> causing Belgium to become the only nation ever to miss a World Cup final round despite not allowing a goal during the qualifiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder2001_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2001-39">[36]</a></sup> The next two attempts to reach a major finals were also fruitless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf76_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf76-40">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf78_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf78-41">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Beginning with a second-place finish at Euro 1980,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf80_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf80-42">[39]</a></sup> the 1980s and the early 1990s are generally considered as Belgium's first golden age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup> Coached by <a href="/wiki/Guy_Thys" title="Guy Thys">Guy Thys</a>, they achieved their spot in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1980_Final" title="UEFA Euro 1980 Final">the 1980 final</a> with an unbeaten record in the group phase; in the final, they narrowly lost the title to West Germany with the score 1–2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf80_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf80-42">[39]</a></sup> Starting with the <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982 World Cup</a>, and ending with the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 World Cup</a>, the national team qualified for six consecutive World Cup end stages and mostly progressed to the second round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC230514_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC230514-44">[41]</a></sup> During this period, managers Guy Thys, Paul Van Himst and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Waseige" title="Robert Waseige">Robert Waseige</a> each guided a Belgian selection past the first round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf82_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf82-45">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf94_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf94-46">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf2002_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf2002-47">[44]</a></sup> In addition to receiving individual <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_awards" title="FIFA World Cup awards">FIFA recognitions</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllStar_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-AllStar-48">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFAWCAwards_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FIFAWCAwards-49">[46]</a></sup> the team reached the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf86_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf86-50">[47]</a></sup> After reaching the Euro 1980 final, they were unsuccessful at subsequent European Championships, with early exits from their appearances at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_1984" title="Euro 1984">Euro 1984</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_2000" title="Euro 2000">Euro 2000</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf84det_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf84det-51">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf2000_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf2000-52">[49]</a></sup> During the late 1990s, they played three friendly tournaments in Morocco, Cyprus and Japan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup> sharing the <a href="/wiki/Kirin_Cup#1999_Kirin_Cup" title="Kirin Cup">1999 Kirin Cup</a> with Peru in the latter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup> The greatest talents of the Belgian team during this golden age were retired from international football by 2000,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllRedD_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-AllRedD-56">[53]</a></sup> yet in 2002, Belgium defeated reigning world and European champions France,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-5"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup> and reached the World Cup round of 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf2002_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf2002-47">[44]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Match_Alg%C3%A9rie_vs_Belgique,_Coupe_du_Monde_2014,_Br%C3%A9sil_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="Belgian defender maneuvering around the Algerian goal" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="429" data-file-width="650" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Match_Alg%C3%A9rie_vs_Belgique%2C_Coupe_du_Monde_2014%2C_Br%C3%A9sil_%28cropped%29.jpg/260px-Match_Alg%C3%A9rie_vs_Belgique%2C_Coupe_du_Monde_2014%2C_Br%C3%A9sil_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Match_Alg%C3%A9rie_vs_Belgique%2C_Coupe_du_Monde_2014%2C_Br%C3%A9sil_%28cropped%29.jpg/390px-Match_Alg%C3%A9rie_vs_Belgique%2C_Coupe_du_Monde_2014%2C_Br%C3%A9sil_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Match_Alg%C3%A9rie_vs_Belgique%2C_Coupe_du_Monde_2014%2C_Br%C3%A9sil_%28cropped%29.jpg/520px-Match_Alg%C3%A9rie_vs_Belgique%2C_Coupe_du_Monde_2014%2C_Br%C3%A9sil_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Match_Alg%C3%A9rie_vs_Belgique,_Coupe_du_Monde_2014,_Br%C3%A9sil_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Belgium <i>(in red)</i> playing <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Mineir%C3%A3o" title="Mineirão">Mineirão</a> in the 2014 World Cup</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the 2002 World Cup, the team weakened with the loss of more veterans and coach Waseige.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[55]</a></sup> They missed out five successive major finals from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_2004" title="Euro 2004">Euro 2004</a> until <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_2012" title="Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a>, and went through an equal number of head coaches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HN060612_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-HN060612-59">[56]</a></sup> A 2005 win over reigning European champions <a href="/wiki/Greece_national_football_team" title="Greece national football team">Greece</a> meant nothing but a small comfort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-6"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup> In between, a promising new generation was maturing at the <a href="/wiki/2007_UEFA_European_Under-21_Championship" title="2007 UEFA European Under-21 Championship">2007 European U-21 Championship</a>; <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_under-21_football_team" title="Belgium national under-21 football team">Belgium's squad</a> qualified for the following year's <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics in Beijing</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[57]</a></sup> where the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2008_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_team_squads#Belgium" title="Football at the 2008 Summer Olympics – Men's team squads">Young Red Devils squad</a> finished fourth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssfOG2008_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssfOG2008-61">[58]</a></sup> Seventeen of them appeared in the senior national team,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllRedD_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-AllRedD-56">[53]</a></sup> albeit without making an immediate impact. Belgium finished in second (and last) place at the <a href="/wiki/Kirin_Cup#2009_Kirin_Cup" title="Kirin Cup">Kirin Cup in May 2009</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup> and lost against the 125th FIFA-ranked <a href="/wiki/Armenia_national_football_team" title="Armenia national football team">Armenian team</a> in September 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFArank_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-FIFArank-3">[2]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/Georges_Leekens" title="Georges Leekens">Georges Leekens</a>' second stint as national manager,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DS130512_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-DS130512-64">[61]</a></sup> his assistant Marc Wilmots became the caretaker in May 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DS150512_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-DS150512-65">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>After two matches as interim coach, Wilmots agreed to replace Leekens as manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DS060612_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-DS060612-66">[63]</a></sup> Following his appointment, the team's results improved,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[64]</a></sup> such that some foreign media regarded it as another Belgian golden generation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2GenUK_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-2GenUK-68">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2GenGER_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-2GenGER-69">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup> The young Belgian squad qualified as unbeaten <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_A" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group A">group winners</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 World Cup</a> finals,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf2014Q_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf2014Q-71">[68]</a></sup> and earned Belgium's second-ever <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup#Tournament_team_rankings" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">place in a World Cup quarter-finals</a> with a four-game winning streak.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf2014_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf2014-72">[69]</a></sup> Belgium qualified for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_2016" title="Euro 2016">Euro 2016</a> with a match to spare in October 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[70]</a></sup> and took the top spot in the FIFA World Rankings for the first time in November 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[71]</a></sup> to stay first for five months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFArank_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-FIFArank-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[72]</a></sup> In the following year, Belgium could not confirm their role as outsider at the European Championship with a quarter-final elimination by the 26th FIFA-ranked <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Welsh team</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFArank_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-FIFArank-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC2016Wal_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-EC2016Wal-76">[73]</a></sup> this prompted the RBFA to dismiss Wilmots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DS150716_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-DS150716-77">[74]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification">2018 World Cup qualifying</a> allocation, they were seeded first in their group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-draw_format_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-draw_format-78">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Kit">Kit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Kit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Belgium_national_football_team#Historical_football_kits" title="History of the Belgium national football team">Historical kits overview</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:460px;max-width:460px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:290px;max-width:290px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BelgiumNFT1980-06-12.jpg"><img alt="Team photo on the pitch" data-file-height="378" data-file-width="570" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/56/BelgiumNFT1980-06-12.jpg/288px-BelgiumNFT1980-06-12.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/56/BelgiumNFT1980-06-12.jpg/432px-BelgiumNFT1980-06-12.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/56/BelgiumNFT1980-06-12.jpg 2x" width="288"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:166px;max-width:166px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Belgium_football_lion_crest.png"><img alt="Team emblem: a gold lion on a black shield background" data-file-height="688" data-file-width="595" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Belgium_football_lion_crest.png/164px-Belgium_football_lion_crest.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Belgium_football_lion_crest.png/246px-Belgium_football_lion_crest.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Belgium_football_lion_crest.png/328px-Belgium_football_lion_crest.png 2x" width="164"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Traditional red jersey worn by the Euro 1980 runners-up, and the stylised lion emblem (1948–80)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In home matches, the team's <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_association_football_terms#O" title="Glossary of association football terms">outfield players</a> traditionally wear the colours of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Belgium" title="Flag of Belgium">Belgian flag</a>: black, yellow and red.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HistFK1_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-HistFK1-81">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GOAAAL80_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-GOAAAL80-82">[79]</a></sup> Red dominates the strip and is often the sole jersey colour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HistFK1_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-HistFK1-81">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GOAAAL80_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-GOAAAL80-82">[79]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Away_colours" title="Away colours">away colours</a> are usually white, black or both;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GOAAAL_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-GOAAAL-83">[80]</a></sup> in 2014, the squad introduced a third, yellow kit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WC2014shirts_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-WC2014shirts-84">[81]</a></sup> Their shirts are often trimmed with <i>tricolores</i> at the margins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GOAAAL80_82-2"><a href="#cite_note-GOAAAL80-82">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GOAAAL70_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-GOAAAL70-85">[82]</a></sup> Since 1981, the RBFA emblem has been the national team's badge;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GOAAAL80_82-3"><a href="#cite_note-GOAAAL80-82">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fotocoll81_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-fotocoll81-86">[83]</a></sup> the previous badge was a yellow lion on a black shield,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HistFK1_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-HistFK1-81">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GOAAAL80_82-4"><a href="#cite_note-GOAAAL80-82">[79]</a></sup> similar to the escutcheon of the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Belgium" title="Coat of arms of Belgium">national coat of arms</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>For their first unofficial match in 1901, the Belgian team wore white jerseys with tricoloured bands on the upper arms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraipontsWillocx2003_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraipontsWillocx2003-14">[12]</a></sup> Around their third unofficial game in 1902, the choice was made for a "shirt with national colours ... [that would indicate,] with a stripe, the number of times every player has participated in an encounter".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHubert198012_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHubert198012-16">[14]</a></sup> Since 1904, Belgium's classic all-red jersey design has been altered twice. In 1904–05, the squad briefly wore satin shirts with three horizontal bands in red, yellow and black; according to sports journalist <a href="/wiki/Victor_Boin" title="Victor Boin">Victor Boin</a>, the shirts set "the ugliness record".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoin1945_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoin1945-21">[19]</a></sup> During the 1970s, manager Raymond Goethals chose an all-white combination to improve the team's visibility during evening matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WhiteDevil_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-WhiteDevil-35">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bruzzz_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-bruzzz-88">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>Six clothing manufacturers have supplied the official team strip. Since 2014, it has been produced by <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[86]</a></sup> who was also the supplier from 1974 to 1980, and from 1982 to 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sponsortimeline_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-sponsortimeline-90">[87]</a></sup> Former kit manufacturers are <a href="/wiki/Umbro" title="Umbro">Umbro</a> (early 1970s),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bruzzz_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-bruzzz-88">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sponsortimeline_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-sponsortimeline-90">[87]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Admiral_Sportswear" title="Admiral Sportswear">Admiral</a> (1981–1982),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[D]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sponsortimeline_90-2"><a href="#cite_note-sponsortimeline-90">[87]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Diadora" title="Diadora">Diadora</a> (1992–1999),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sponsortimeline_90-3"><a href="#cite_note-sponsortimeline-90">[87]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a> (1999–2010) and <a href="/wiki/BURRDA" title="BURRDA">BURRDA</a> (2010–2014).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[E]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sponsortimeline_90-4"><a href="#cite_note-sponsortimeline-90">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_stadium">Home stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Home stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team_home_stadium" title="Belgium national football team home stadium">Belgium national football team home stadium</a> and <a href="/wiki/King_Baudouin_Stadium" title="King Baudouin Stadium">King Baudouin Stadium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:486px;max-width:486px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:262px;max-width:262px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JubileeStadium1935.jpg"><img alt="Aerial photo of packed stadium" data-file-height="493" data-file-width="794" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/JubileeStadium1935.jpg/260px-JubileeStadium1935.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/JubileeStadium1935.jpg/390px-JubileeStadium1935.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/JubileeStadium1935.jpg/520px-JubileeStadium1935.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:220px;max-width:220px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stade_Roi_Baudouin.JPG"><img alt="Stadium interior, photographed from the grandstand" data-file-height="2037" data-file-width="2761" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Stade_Roi_Baudouin.JPG/218px-Stade_Roi_Baudouin.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Stade_Roi_Baudouin.JPG/327px-Stade_Roi_Baudouin.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Stade_Roi_Baudouin.JPG/436px-Stade_Roi_Baudouin.JPG 2x" width="218"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">The national stadium at the Heysel Plateau in 1935 <i>(left)</i> and in 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Numerous former and current <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team_home_stadium#List_of_home_stadiums" title="Belgium national football team home stadium">venues in 11 urban areas</a> have hosted Belgium's home games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-7"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup> Most of these matches have been played in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Heysel_Plateau" title="Heysel Plateau">Heysel Plateau</a>, on the site of the present-day King Baudouin Stadium—a multipurpose facility with a seating capacity of 50,122.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[90]</a></sup> Its field also hosts the team's final trainings before domestic games. Since 2007, most physical preparation takes place at the National Football Centre in <a href="/wiki/Tubize" title="Tubize">Tubize</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[91]</a></sup> or at <a href="/wiki/R.S.C._Anderlecht" title="R.S.C. Anderlecht">Anderlecht</a>'s training ground in the <a href="/wiki/Anderlecht" title="Anderlecht">Neerpede</a> quarter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[93]</a></sup> Apart from Belgian home friendlies, at the international level Belgium's national stadium has also hosted six European Championship games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1930, for the country's centennial, the venue was inaugurated as the Jubilee Stadium with an unofficial match between Belgium and the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DerbyBelNed_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-DerbyBelNed-101">[96]</a></sup> At that time, the stadium had a capacity of 75,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[97]</a></sup> In 1946, it was renamed Heysel Stadium after its city quarter. This new name became associated with the tragedy preceding the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1985_European_Cup_final" title="1985 European Cup final">1985 European Cup final</a> between Juventus and Liverpool; <a href="/wiki/Heysel_Stadium_disaster" title="Heysel Stadium disaster">39 spectators died</a> after riots in the then antiquated building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParrishNauright2014xxviii_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParrishNauright2014xxviii-104">[99]</a></sup> Three years after the disaster, plans were unveiled for a renovation;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[100]</a></sup> in 1995, after two years of work, the modernised stadium was named after the late <a href="/wiki/Baudouin_of_Belgium" title="Baudouin of Belgium">King Baudouin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[101]</a></sup> In May 2013, the Brussels-Capital Region announced that the King Baudouin Stadium would be replaced by <a href="/wiki/Eurostadium" title="Eurostadium">Eurostadium</a>, elsewhere on the Heysel Plateau;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[102]</a></sup> two years later, a 2019 date was set for the stadium's completion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_image">Team image</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Team image">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">Media coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Media coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gust_De_Muynck_Belgium-Netherlands_1931.jpg"><img alt="Journalist, seated in the stands and speaking into a microphone" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="359" data-file-width="500" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Gust_De_Muynck_Belgium-Netherlands_1931.jpg/260px-Gust_De_Muynck_Belgium-Netherlands_1931.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Gust_De_Muynck_Belgium-Netherlands_1931.jpg/390px-Gust_De_Muynck_Belgium-Netherlands_1931.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/ba/Gust_De_Muynck_Belgium-Netherlands_1931.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gust_De_Muynck_Belgium-Netherlands_1931.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gust De Muynck's live coverage during Belgium–Netherlands in 1931</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first live coverage of a Belgian sporting event occurred on 3 May 1931, when journalist <a href="/wiki/Gust_De_Muynck" title="Gust De Muynck">Gust De Muynck</a> commentated on the football game between Belgium and the Netherlands on radio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[104]</a></sup> Later, football broadcasts were also televised. As 60 per cent of Belgians speak Dutch and 40 per cent French,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA-Bel_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-Bel-110">[105]</a></sup> commentaries for the national team matches are provided in both languages. The games are not broadcast in German—Belgium's third official language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA-Bel_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-Bel-110">[105]</a></sup> During Belgium's tournament appearances in the 1980s and the early 1990s, <a href="/wiki/Rik_De_Saedeleer" title="Rik De Saedeleer">Rik De Saedeleer</a> crowned himself the nation's most famous football commentator with his emotional and humorous reports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>Initially the matches were transmitted mainly on public television channels: the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BRTN" title="BRTN">BRTN</a> in Dutch, and the <a href="/wiki/RTBF" title="RTBF">RTBF</a> in French. Since 1994, commercial channels such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vtm" title="Vtm">vtm</a> and its sister channel <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kanaal_2" title="Kanaal 2">Kanaal 2</a>, and <a href="/wiki/VIER" title="VIER">VIER</a> in <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a>, have purchased broadcasting rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RBFAhist_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-RBFAhist-1">[1]</a></sup> As of November 2016, the Euro 2016 <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_knockout_phase#Hungary_vs_Belgium" title="UEFA Euro 2016 knockout phase">round-of-16 match against Hungary</a> was the most-watched programme in Belgian television history, with an audience of over four million viewers out of 11.3 million Belgian citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA-Bel_110-2"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-Bel-110">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Vlaamse_Radio-_en_Televisieomroeporganisatie" title="Vlaamse Radio- en Televisieomroeporganisatie">VRT</a> started transmitting a nine-piece, behind-the-scenes documentary about the national team filmed during the 2014 World Cup qualifiers, titled <i>Iedereen Duivel</i> (<i>Everybody Devil</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[109]</a></sup> Cable broadband provider <a href="/wiki/Telenet_(Belgium)" title="Telenet (Belgium)">Telenet</a> broadcast an eight-part documentary about individual players titled <i>Rode Helden</i> (<i>Red Heroes</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Side_activities">Side activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Side activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:France-Belgium_1918-04-21.jpg"><img alt="Old cartoon of an association football match with the goalkeeper in the middle who jumps and hits the ball" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1334" data-file-width="1391" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/France-Belgium_1918-04-21.jpg/260px-France-Belgium_1918-04-21.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/France-Belgium_1918-04-21.jpg/390px-France-Belgium_1918-04-21.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/France-Belgium_1918-04-21.jpg/520px-France-Belgium_1918-04-21.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:France-Belgium_1918-04-21.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Illustration of Belgium's game against France in April 1918. Some of these unofficial wartime matches served as charity fundraisers.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Multiple events were organised for the fans during the squad's peak popularity in the 2010s. During the 2014 World Cup qualifiers, a string of interactive events called the <i>Devil Challenges</i> were organised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[111]</a></sup> The premise was that small groups of international players would do a favour in return for each of the five comprehensive chores their supporters completed ("colour Belgium red", "gather 500,000 decibels", etc.), all of which were accomplished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[112]</a></sup> In June 2013, the Belgian national team's first ever Fan Day attracted over 20,000 supporters;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HLN020613_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-HLN020613-118">[113]</a></sup> a second was held after the 2014 World Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[114]</a></sup> On the days of Belgium's 2014 World Cup group matches, large dance events titled <i>Dance with the Devils</i> took place in three Belgian cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[115]</a></sup> This type of happening was repeated during Belgium's Euro 2016 group matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Occasionally, the Belgian team directly supported charity. Between 1914 and 1941 they played at minimum five unofficial games of which the returns were for charitable purposes: two against France,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DT210316_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-DT210316-26">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FraBelWWIa_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FraBelWWIa-122">[117]</a></sup> and three against the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DerbyBelNed_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-DerbyBelNed-101">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BelNed1941_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-BelNed1941-123">[118]</a></sup> In mid-1986, when the Belgian delegation reached the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">Mexico World Cup</a> semi-finals, the squad started a project titled Casa Hogar, an idea of delegation leader <a href="/wiki/Michel_D%27Hooghe" title="Michel D'Hooghe">Michel D'Hooghe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[119]</a></sup> Casa Hogar is a home for street children in the Mexican industrial city of <a href="/wiki/Toluca" title="Toluca">Toluca</a>, to which the footballers donated part of their tournament bonuses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[120]</a></sup> In August 2013, the national team supported four social projects through the charity fund Football+ Foundation, by playing an A-match with a plus sign on the shoulders of their jerseys and auctioning the shirts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2002, the national squad held its first <a href="/wiki/Anti-racism" title="Anti-racism">anti-racism</a> campaign in which they posed with slogans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[122]</a></sup> A home Euro 2012 qualifier was given the theme of respect for diversity in 2010; this UEFA-supported action was part of the European <a href="/wiki/Football_Against_Racism_in_Europe" title="Football Against Racism in Europe">FARE</a> Action Week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[123]</a></sup> Ex-Red Devil <a href="/wiki/Dimitri_Mbuyu" title="Dimitri Mbuyu">Dimitri Mbuyu</a>—the first black Belgium player (in 1987)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllRedD_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-AllRedD-56">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[124]</a></sup>—was engaged as godfather, and other foreign, current, and former footballers who played in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgian_Pro_League" title="Belgian Pro League">Belgian top division</a> participated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[125]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nickname_and_logo">Nickname and logo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Nickname and logo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After a 1905 match, a Dutch reporter wrote that three Belgian footballers "work[ed] as devils".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RN160505_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-RN160505-131">[126]</a></sup> A year later <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9opold_FC" title="Léopold FC">Léopold FC</a> manager Pierre Walckiers nicknamed the players Red Devils, inspired by their jersey colour, and the achievement of three successive victories in 1906.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuldemontDeps199565_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuldemontDeps199565-22">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-8"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup> Because of their white home shirts in the 1970s, they were temporarily known as the White Devils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WhiteDevil_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-WhiteDevil-35">[32]</a></sup> Since 2012, the team logo is a red trident (or three-pronged pitchfork),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[127]</a></sup> an item that is often associated with the devil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERussell1987129_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERussell1987129-133">[128]</a></sup> Before that, the national squad had three official <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphism" title="Anthropomorphism">anthropomorphous</a> mascots. The first was a lion in team kit named Diabolix,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mascot_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-mascot-134">[129]</a></sup> a reference to the central symbol in the Belgian coat of arms that appeared on the team jerseys from 1905 to 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GOAAAL80_82-5"><a href="#cite_note-GOAAAL80-82">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fotocoll1905_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-fotocoll1905-135">[130]</a></sup> In accordance with their epithet, the next mascots were a red super-devil and a fan-made modern devil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mascot_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-mascot-134">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporters">Supporters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Supporters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:250px; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #c6dbf7;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Cycling is the traditional national sport of Belgium, but soccer is the most popular."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—Historian Richard Henshaw, 1979<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197975_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197975-11">[9]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>Fans of the Belgian national team display the country's tricolour national flag, usually with an emphasis on the red element. In 2012, local supporter clubs merged into one large Belgian federation named "1895" after the foundation year of the RBFA. One year later, 1895 had 24,000 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[131]</a></sup> The nationwide interest in the football squad has also been reflected by the occasional presence of <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Belgium" title="Monarchy of Belgium">Belgian monarchs</a> at their matches since 1914.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[134]</a></sup> One of the greatest moments for the Belgian team and their <a href="/wiki/12th_man_(football)" title="12th man (football)">12th man</a> was in mid-1986 when the Belgian delegation at the Mexico World Cup received a warm "welcome home". When the World Cup semi-finalists appeared on the balcony of <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Town_Hall" title="Brussels Town Hall">Brussels Town Hall</a>, the adjoining Grand Place square was filled with an ecstatic crowd that cheered as though their squad had won a major tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[135]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Belgium_supporters%27_club_1895.gif"><img alt="Number 1895 in red and bold, with the digit 9 carrying devil's horns and tail" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="249" data-file-width="387" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b5/Belgium_supporters%27_club_1895.gif/220px-Belgium_supporters%27_club_1895.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b5/Belgium_supporters%27_club_1895.gif/330px-Belgium_supporters%27_club_1895.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b5/Belgium_supporters%27_club_1895.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Belgium_supporters%27_club_1895.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Logo of the national fan federation</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The team's deterioration after the 2002 World Cup lead to their absence from the end stages of the next five major tournaments, and strained their popularity. Between 2004 and 2010, local journalists called the Belgian footballing nation "mortally ill".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[137]</a></sup> Some fans continued to support their squad in bad times. Ludo Rollenberg was one of the most loyal fans attending the team's games worldwide since 1990, missing only the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Kirin_Cup" title="Kirin Cup">Kirin Cup</a> in 1999, and two other matches by 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[138]</a></sup> He was the only supporter to attend their game in Armenia in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Just before the kick-off of a 2014 World Cup home qualifier, Belgium's footballers saw a first <a href="/wiki/Tifo" title="Tifo">tifo</a> banner, sized 10.5 by 11.5 metres (34 by 38 ft) depicting a devil in the national colours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[140]</a></sup> The presence of many Belgian players in top leagues abroad, such as the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWillems2013_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWillems2013-146">[141]</a></sup> and promising results under Marc Wilmots, increased fans' enthusiasm and belief in a successful World Cup campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HLN020613_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-HLN020613-118">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[142]</a></sup> Because of this popularity peak, two Belgian monuments were decorated in national colours for the 2014 FIFA World Cup event; the <a href="/wiki/Manneken_Pis" title="Manneken Pis">Manneken Pis</a> statue received a child-sized version of the new Belgian uniform,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[143]</a></sup> and facets of the <a href="/wiki/Atomium" title="Atomium">Atomium</a>'s upper sphere were covered in black, yellow and red vinyl.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[144]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries_derby" title="Low Countries derby">Low Countries derby</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1905RNBmoment(2).jpg"><img alt="Match phase with two outfield players from each side" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="664" data-file-width="1400" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/1905RNBmoment%282%29.jpg/290px-1905RNBmoment%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/1905RNBmoment%282%29.jpg/435px-1905RNBmoment%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/1905RNBmoment%282%29.jpg/580px-1905RNBmoment%282%29.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1905RNBmoment(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Illustration of a Netherlands–Belgium cup match at Rotterdam's Schuttersveld pitch in 1905</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Belgium's main football rivals are its neighbours the Netherlands and France, with which it shares close cultural and political relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[146]</a></sup> The matchup between the Belgian and <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Dutch team</a> is known as the Low Countries <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_association_football_terms#D" title="Glossary of association football terms">derby</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DerbyBelNed_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-DerbyBelNed-101">[96]</a></sup> as of November 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> they have played each other in 126 official games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFAcomp_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-FIFAcomp-152">[147]</a></sup> The clash between the Belgian and French sides is nicknamed <i>le Match Sympathique</i> in French ("the Friendly Match");<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[148]</a></sup> they have contested 73 official games as of November 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFAcomp_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-FIFAcomp-152">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>Belgium won the first four—unofficial—matches against the Netherlands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHubert198012_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHubert198012-16">[14]</a></sup> but lost their first FIFA-recognised contest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-9"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup> The two national teams played each other biannually between 1905 and 1964, except during the World Wars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-10"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup> They have met 18 times in major tournament campaigns, and have played at least <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries_derby#Belgium_vs._Netherlands_Cups" title="Low Countries derby">35 friendly cup matches</a>: in Belgium for the <i>Coupe Vanden Abeele</i>, and in the Netherlands for the <i>Rotterdamsch Nieuwsblad-Beker</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TrouwCVA_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-TrouwCVA-15">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RN160505_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-RN160505-131">[126]</a></sup> The overall balance favours the Netherlands, with 55 wins against 41 Belgian victories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFAcomp_152-2"><a href="#cite_note-FIFAcomp-152">[147]</a></sup> The Low Countries' squads co-operated in fundraising initiatives between 1925 and 1941; they played five unofficial games for charity, FIFA and the Belgian Olympic Committee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DerbyBelNed_101-3"><a href="#cite_note-DerbyBelNed-101">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BelNed1941_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-BelNed1941-123">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first match between Belgium and France, the <i>Évence Coppée</i> Trophy played in 1904, was the first official game for both teams and the first official football match between independent countries on the European continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[150]</a></sup> Until 1967, the sides met almost annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-11"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup> As of November 2016, France has played most often against Belgium in international football.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFAcomp_152-3"><a href="#cite_note-FIFAcomp-152">[147]</a></sup> Belgium have the better record, with 30 wins to France's 24.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFAcomp_152-4"><a href="#cite_note-FIFAcomp-152">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Management">Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Belgium_national_football_team_managers" title="List of Belgium national football team managers">List of Belgium national football team managers</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martinez_Roberto_126181_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="Portrait of a seriously-looking shaved man in coat" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="385" data-file-width="410" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Martinez_Roberto_126181_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Martinez_Roberto_126181_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Martinez_Roberto_126181_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Martinez_Roberto_126181_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4b/Martinez_Roberto_126181_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Martinez_Roberto_126181_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Roberto Martínez, Belgium's current head coach (since 2016)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since 1904, the RBFA, 24 permanent managers and two caretaker managers have officially been in charge of the national team;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[F]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manrsssf_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-manrsssf-23">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HN060612_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-HN060612-59">[56]</a></sup> this includes one national footballer selector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manrsssf_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-manrsssf-23">[21]</a></sup> As of November 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, a crew of over 20 RBFA employees guides the player group,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[153]</a></sup> including their Spanish manager <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Roberto Martínez">Roberto Martínez</a>, his assistants <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Jones" title="Graeme Jones">Graeme Jones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Henry" title="Thierry Henry">Thierry Henry</a>, and goalkeeping coaches <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Lemmens" title="Erwin Lemmens">Erwin Lemmens</a> and <a href="/wiki/I%C3%B1aki_Bergara" title="Iñaki Bergara">Iñaki Bergara</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[155]</a></sup> As of 13 November 2016, Marc Wilmots is statistically the best performing Belgium manager with an average of 2.18 points per match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[G]</a></sup> Under him, Belgium reached the top FIFA ranking spot in 2015, which earned him the title of Best Coach of the Year at the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Globe_Soccer_Awards" title="Globe Soccer Awards">Globe Soccer Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[156]</a></sup> Under Guy Thys, the squad achieved record results at World and European championships; <a href="/wiki/World_Soccer_(magazine)" title="World Soccer (magazine)"><i>World Soccer</i> magazine</a> accordingly proclaimed him Manager of the Year in 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rather than developing innovative team formations or styles of play, Belgium's managers applied conventional tactics. At the three 1930s World Cups, the Red Devils were aligned in a contemporary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2%E2%80%933%E2%80%935" title="2–3–5">2–3–5 "pyramid"</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf30_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf30-165">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf34_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf34-166">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf38_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf38-167">[160]</a></sup> In 1954, <a href="/wiki/Doug_Livingstone" title="Doug Livingstone">Doug Livingstone</a>'s squad played in a <a href="/wiki/Formation_(association_football)#WM" title="Formation (association football)">3–2–5 "WM" arrangement</a> during World Cup matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf54_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf54-32">[29]</a></sup> Throughout most of their tournament games in the 1970s, the 1980s and the 1990s, the team played in a <a href="/wiki/Formation_(association_football)#4.E2.80.934.E2.80.932" title="Formation (association football)">4–4–2 formation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf70_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf70-36">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf82_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf82-45">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf94_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf94-46">[43]</a></sup> Since Raymond Goethals' stint in the 1970s, a key strength of the Belgian squad has been their systematic use of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Offside_trap" title="Offside trap">offside trap</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[161]</a></sup> a defensive tactic that was already intensively applied in the 1960s by Anderlecht coach <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Sinibaldi" title="Pierre Sinibaldi">Pierre Sinibaldi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[162]</a></sup> According to football journalist Wim De Bock, "master tactician" Goethals represented the "conservative, defensive football of the Belgian national team"; he added that in the 1970s, the contrast between the Belgian playing style and the <a href="/wiki/Total_Football" title="Total Football">Total Football</a> of their Dutch rivals "could not be bigger".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Bock2013_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Bock2013-170">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an attempt to win a game at the 1998 World Cup, Georges Leekens chose a <a href="/wiki/Formation_(association_football)#4.E2.80.933.E2.80.933" title="Formation (association football)">4–3–3</a> arrangement for Belgium's second and third group matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf98_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf98-171">[164]</a></sup> Robert Waseige, Belgium coach around 2000, said that "above all, [his] 4–4–2 system [was] holy", in the sense that he left good attackers on the bench to keep his favourite formation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[165]</a></sup> Wilmots opted for the 4–3–3 line-up again,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[166]</a></sup> with the intention of showing dominant football against any country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[167]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Players">Players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Belgium_international_footballers" title="List of Belgium international footballers">List of Belgium international footballers</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Belgium_national_football_team_captains" title="List of Belgium national football team captains">List of Belgium national football team captains</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following 23 players were convocated for the friendly against the Netherlands and the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_H" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group H">2018 World Cup qualifier</a> against <a href="/wiki/Estonia_national_football_team" title="Estonia national football team">Estonia</a>, on 9 and 11 November respectively,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rbfa_selection_20161104_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-rbfa_selection_20161104-175">[168]</a></sup> and were able to play in the latter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DS081116_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-DS081116-176">[169]</a></sup> Leander Dendoncker was called up to replace the injuries of Moussa Dembélé and Vincent Kompany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SP111116_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-SP111116-177">[170]</a></sup> Following the injury of Christian Kabasele, Timmy Simons was called up to replace him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SP131116_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-SP131116-178">[171]</a></sup> Note that the RBFA lists all wingers as forwards.</p>
<p><small>Caps and goals are correct as of 13 November 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> after the game against Estonia;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[172]</a></sup> only FIFA-recognised matches are included.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fifa_unrec_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-fifa_unrec-181">[H]</a></sup></small></p>
