<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-greek;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable">Notable</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Notable">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PaulVanHimst1964.jpg"><img alt="Player on the pitch in national team outfit" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="483" data-file-width="304" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/PaulVanHimst1964.jpg/160px-PaulVanHimst1964.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/PaulVanHimst1964.jpg/240px-PaulVanHimst1964.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/38/PaulVanHimst1964.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PaulVanHimst1964.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paul Van Himst</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Between 1904 and 1980, mainly attacking Belgium players were recognised as talented footballers. In the team's first decade, striker <a href="/wiki/Robert_De_Veen" title="Robert De Veen">Robert De Veen</a> was very productive with 26 goals in 23 international appearances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSSSF_BelIntRec_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-RSSSF_BelIntRec-188">[180]</a></sup> Richard Henshaw described <a href="/wiki/Alphonse_Six" title="Alphonse Six">Alphonse Six</a> as "Belgium's greatest player in the prewar period ... [who] was often called the most skillful forward outside Great Britain".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197976_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197976-28">[25]</a></sup> The key player of the victorious 1920 Olympic squad was <a href="/wiki/Robert_Copp%C3%A9e" title="Robert Coppée">Robert Coppée</a>, who scored a <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick#Association_football" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> against Spain's <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Zamora" title="Ricardo Zamora">Ricardo Zamora</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFA1920_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-FIFA1920-189">[181]</a></sup> and the penalty in the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1920finalFIFA_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-1920finalFIFA-190">[182]</a></sup> Other outstanding Belgian strikers in the interwar period were top scorer <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Voorhoof" title="Bernard Voorhoof">Bernard Voorhoof</a> and "Belgium's football grandmaster" <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Braine" title="Raymond Braine">Raymond Braine</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllRedD_56-3"><a href="#cite_note-AllRedD-56">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[183]</a></sup> considered "one of the greatest players of the era".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMurray199863_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurray199863-192">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gifted players in the 1940s and the 1950s included <a href="/wiki/Defender_(association_football)" title="Defender (association football)">centre-back</a> <a href="/wiki/Louis_Carr%C3%A9" title="Louis Carré">Louis Carré</a> and attackers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jef_Mermans" title="Jef Mermans">Jef Mermans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pol_Anoul" title="Pol Anoul">Pol Anoul</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rik_Coppens" title="Rik Coppens">Rik Coppens</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197976_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197976-28">[25]</a></sup> at the 1954 World Cup, Anoul shone with three goals,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf54_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf54-32">[29]</a></sup> and newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/L%27%C3%89quipe" title="L'Équipe">L'Équipe</a></i> named Coppens the event's best centre forward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[185]</a></sup> The 1960s and the early 1970s were the glory days of forward and four-time <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Golden_Shoe" title="Belgian Golden Shoe">Belgian Golden Shoe</a> Paul Van Himst,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GoScho_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-GoScho-194">[186]</a></sup> later elected Belgian <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Jubilee_Awards" title="UEFA Jubilee Awards">UEFA Golden Player</a> of 1954–2003 and Belgium's Player of the Century by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IFFHS" title="IFFHS">IFFHS</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[188]</a></sup> At the 1965 <a href="/wiki/Ballon_d%27Or" title="Ballon d'Or">Ballon d'Or</a>, Van Himst ranked fourth, achieving Belgium's highest ever position at the European football election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[189]</a></sup> Decades after Coppens and Van Himst had retired from playing football, a journalist on a Flemish television show asked them "Who [from both of you] was the best, actually?". Coppens replied: "I will ask Paul that ... If Paul says it was me, then he's right".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[190]</a></sup> In 1966, striker <a href="/wiki/Raoul_Lambert" title="Raoul Lambert">Raoul Lambert</a> and defending midfielder <a href="/wiki/Wilfried_Van_Moer" title="Wilfried Van Moer">Wilfried Van Moer</a> joined the national team;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllRedD_56-4"><a href="#cite_note-AllRedD-56">[53]</a></sup> while the UEFA praised Lambert for his skills at Euro 1972,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[191]</a></sup> Van Moer won three Golden Shoes and equalled Van Himst's fourth rank at the Ballon d'Or in 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GoScho_194-1"><a href="#cite_note-GoScho-194">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[192]</a></sup></p>
<p>Belgium has seen two talented waves since 1980, from which several players in defensive positions gained international fame. In the 1980s and the early 1990s, goalkeepers <a href="/wiki/Jean-Marie_Pfaff" title="Jean-Marie Pfaff">Jean-Marie Pfaff</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michel_Preud%27homme" title="Michel Preud'homme">Michel Preud'homme</a> were elected best <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_association_football_terms#C" title="Glossary of association football terms">custodians</a> at FIFA World Cups,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllStar_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-AllStar-48">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFAWCAwards_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-FIFAWCAwards-49">[46]</a></sup> while FIFA recognised midfielders <a href="/wiki/Jan_Ceulemans" title="Jan Ceulemans">Jan Ceulemans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Enzo_Scifo" title="Enzo Scifo">Enzo Scifo</a> as the propelling forces of Belgium's 1986 FIFA World Cup squad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllStar_48-2"><a href="#cite_note-AllStar-48">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[193]</a></sup> In 2002, after all players of this generation had retired,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllRedD_56-5"><a href="#cite_note-AllRedD-56">[53]</a></sup> Marc Wilmots became Belgium's top scorer at the World Cup with five goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf2002_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf2002-47">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf98_171-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf98-171">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 12 years in which Belgium failed to qualify for major tournaments, another golden generation matured, most of whom later featured in foreign top football leagues; as of July 2013, 12 Belgian national team players would play the next season in the English Premier League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWillems2013_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWillems2013-146">[141]</a></sup> Five players of this generation gained both prime individual and team awards in foreign top competitions or European club competitions:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[I]</a></sup> defenders <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Kompany" title="Vincent Kompany">Vincent Kompany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jan_Vertonghen" title="Jan Vertonghen">Jan Vertonghen</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoccerwayKompany_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-SoccerwayKompany-204">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC290413_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC290413-205">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoccerwayVertonghen_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-SoccerwayVertonghen-206">[197]</a></sup> wingers <a href="/wiki/Eden_Hazard" title="Eden Hazard">Eden Hazard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_De_Bruyne" title="Kevin De Bruyne">Kevin De Bruyne</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PLEHazard_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-PLEHazard-207">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoccerwayEHazard_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-SoccerwayEHazard-208">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SporzaDeBruyne_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-SporzaDeBruyne-209">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoccerwayDeBruyne_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-SoccerwayDeBruyne-210">[201]</a></sup> and forward <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Mirallas" title="Kevin Mirallas">Kevin Mirallas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoccerwayMirallas_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-SoccerwayMirallas-212">[203]</a></sup> However, as of November 2016 none of them were regarded by FIFA or UEFA to be the best at their position in any major international tournament yet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Euro2016DreamTeam_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-Euro2016DreamTeam-214">[205]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitive_record">Competitive record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Competitive record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team_records#Achievements" title="Belgium national football team records">Belgium national football team records § Achievements</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team_results" title="Belgium national football team results">Belgium national football team results</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FIFA_World_Cup">FIFA World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: FIFA World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Belgium_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup" title="Belgium at the FIFA World Cup">Belgium at the FIFA World Cup</a></div>
<p>Belgium failed to progress past the first round of their earliest five World Cup participations. After two scoreless defeats at the <a href="/wiki/1930_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1930 FIFA World Cup">inaugural World Cup</a> in 1930,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf30_165-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf30-165">[158]</a></sup> the team scored in their first-round knockout games in <a href="/wiki/1934_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1934 FIFA World Cup">the 1934</a> and <a href="/wiki/1938_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1938 FIFA World Cup">1938 editions</a>—but only enough to save their honour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf34_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf34-166">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf38_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf38-167">[160]</a></sup> In 1954, they tied with England (4–4 after extra time),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf54_32-3"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf54-32">[29]</a></sup> and in 1970, they won their first World Cup match, against <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador_national_football_team" title="El Salvador national football team">El Salvador</a> (3–0).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf70_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf70-36">[33]</a></sup> From 1982 until 2002, Belgium reached six successive World Cups by playing qualification rounds, advancing to the second phase five times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC230514_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC230514-44">[41]</a></sup> In the 1982 FIFA World Cup opener, Belgium beat defending champions Argentina 1–0. Their tournament ended in the second group stage, after a <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">Polish</a> hat-trick by <a href="/wiki/Zbigniew_Boniek" title="Zbigniew Boniek">Zbigniew Boniek</a> and a 0–1 loss against the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_national_football_team" title="Soviet Union national football team">Soviet Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf82_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf82-45">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eeuubelgica1930.JPG"><img alt="Match phase with aerial play" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="522" data-file-width="858" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Eeuubelgica1930.JPG/260px-Eeuubelgica1930.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Eeuubelgica1930.JPG/390px-Eeuubelgica1930.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Eeuubelgica1930.JPG/520px-Eeuubelgica1930.JPG 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eeuubelgica1930.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
United States–Belgium in 1930 was the joint first ever World Cup match.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At Mexico 1986, the Belgian team achieved their best-ever World Cup run. In the knockout phase as <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_association_football_terms#U" title="Glossary of association football terms">underdogs</a> they beat the Soviets after <a href="/wiki/Overtime_(sports)" title="Overtime (sports)">extra time</a> (3–4);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[206]</a></sup> the unnoticed offside position of Jan Ceulemans, during the initial ninety minutes, allowed him to <a href="/wiki/Equaliser_(sports)" title="Equaliser (sports)">equalise</a> (2–2) and force the game into extra time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[207]</a></sup> They also beat <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a>, in a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shoot-out</a> after a 1–1 draw, but lost to eventual champions Argentina in the semi-final 2–0, and France in the third-place match (4–2).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf86_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf86-50">[47]</a></sup> In the 1990 FIFA World Cup, Belgium dominated periods of their second-round match against England;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEdworthy1997138.E2.80.93139_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdworthy1997138.E2.80.93139-217">[208]</a></sup> Enzo Scifo and Jan Ceulemans hit the <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_association_football_terms#W" title="Glossary of association football terms">woodwork</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[209]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Platt_(footballer)" title="David Platt (footballer)">David Platt</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volley_(football)" title="Volley (football)">volley</a> in the final minute of extra time, described as "nearly blind" by Richard Witzig,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWitzig2006167_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitzig2006167-219">[210]</a></sup> avoided an apparently goalless draw and led to the sudden elimination of the Belgians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf90_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf90-220">[211]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1994, a 3–2 defeat to defending champions <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> saw Belgium go out in the second round again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf94_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf94-46">[43]</a></sup> Afterwards, the entire Belgian delegation criticised referee <a href="/wiki/Kurt_R%C3%B6thlisberger" title="Kurt Röthlisberger">Kurt Röthlisberger</a> for not awarding a penalty for a <a href="/wiki/Fouls_and_misconduct_(association_football)" title="Fouls and misconduct (association football)">foul</a> on Belgian <a href="/wiki/Josip_Weber" title="Josip Weber">Josip Weber</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[212]</a></sup> Three draws in the group stage of the 1998 World Cup were insufficient for Belgium to reach the knockout stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf98_171-2"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf98-171">[164]</a></sup> With two draws, the 2002 FIFA World Cup started poorly for Belgium, but they won the decisive group match against Russia 3–2. In the second round, they faced eventual World Cup winners Brazil; Belgium lost 2–0 after Marc Wilmots' headed opening goal was disallowed due to a "phantom foul" on <a href="/wiki/Roque_J%C3%BAnior" title="Roque Júnior">Roque Júnior</a>, as Witzig named it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf2002_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf2002-47">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWitzig2006289_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitzig2006289-222">[213]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, Belgium beat all their group opponents with a single-goal difference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf2014_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf2014-72">[69]</a></sup> Thereafter, they played an entertaining round of 16 game against the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">United States</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[214]</a></sup> in which American goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Tim_Howard" title="Tim Howard">Tim Howard</a> made 15 saves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[J]</a></sup> However, they defeated the US 2–1 in extra time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf2014_72-2"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf2014-72">[69]</a></sup> In a balanced quarter-final, Argentina eliminated Belgium, after a 1–0 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[216]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UEFA_European_Championship">UEFA European Championship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: UEFA European Championship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgium_at_the_UEFA_European_Football_Championship" title="Belgium at the UEFA European Football Championship">Belgium at the UEFA European Football Championship</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1980-RFA-BEL_1980-FIN-Euro.svg"><img alt="Scheme of football pitch with the line-ups of a red team in 4-4-2 formation against a white team in 5-3-2 formation" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="738" data-file-width="534" height="304" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/1980-RFA-BEL_1980-FIN-Euro.svg/220px-1980-RFA-BEL_1980-FIN-Euro.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/1980-RFA-BEL_1980-FIN-Euro.svg/330px-1980-RFA-BEL_1980-FIN-Euro.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/1980-RFA-BEL_1980-FIN-Euro.svg/440px-1980-RFA-BEL_1980-FIN-Euro.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1980-RFA-BEL_1980-FIN-Euro.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Line-ups of the Euro 1980 final: Belgium <i>(red)</i> against West Germany</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With four successful qualification campaigns out of thirteen, Belgium's performance in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">European Championship</a> does not compare to their World Cup record. Belgium has hosted or co-hosted the event twice; they were chosen to accommodate the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1972_European_Football_Championship" title="1972 European Football Championship">1972 European Football Championship</a> from three candidates,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[K]</a></sup> and hosted <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000" title="UEFA Euro 2000">UEFA Euro 2000</a> with the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf2000_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf2000-52">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>At Euro 1972, Belgium finished third after losing 1–2 against West Germany and beating Hungary 2–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf72_37-3"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf72-37">[34]</a></sup> The team's best continental result is their second place at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1980_European_Football_Championship" title="1980 European Football Championship">Euro 1980</a> in Italy. By finishing as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1980_Group_B" title="UEFA Euro 1980 Group B">group winners</a>, Belgium reached <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1980_Final" title="UEFA Euro 1980 Final">the final</a>, to face West Germany. The West German <a href="/wiki/Horst_Hrubesch" title="Horst Hrubesch">Horst Hrubesch</a> scored first, but <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Vandereycken" title="René Vandereycken">René Vandereycken</a> equalised courtesy of a penalty. Two minutes before the regular playing time ended, Hrubesch scored again denying Belgium a first European title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf80_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf80-42">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>At Euro 1984, in their last and decisive group match against <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a>, the Belgian team took a 0–2 lead, but the Danes won the match 3–2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf84det_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf84det-51">[48]</a></sup> Sixteen years later, Belgium automatically reappeared at UEFA's national team tournament as co-hosts. After winning the Euro 2000 opener against <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a> 2–1,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[219]</a></sup> two 2–0 losses against eventual runners-up Italy and <a href="/wiki/Turkey_national_football_team" title="Turkey national football team">Turkey</a> eliminated the Belgians from the tournament by the end of the group stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf2000_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf2000-52">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>In spite of winning with broad margins against the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a> (3–0) and <a href="/wiki/Hungary_national_football_team" title="Hungary national football team">Hungary</a> (0–4) at Euro 2016,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[220]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[221]</a></sup> Belgium's second very talented generation disappointed with a quarter-final exit. As during the tournament's qualifiers, Wales got the better of Belgium, with a 3–1 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC2016Wal_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-EC2016Wal-76">[73]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Summer_Olympic_Games">Summer Olympic Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Summer Olympic Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Belgium_at_the_Olympics" title="Belgium at the Olympics">Belgium at the Olympics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BEL-LUX_SO1928.JPG"><img alt="Aerial play with two Belgian players and the Luxembourg keeper trying to touch the ball" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="451" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/BEL-LUX_SO1928.JPG/260px-BEL-LUX_SO1928.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/BEL-LUX_SO1928.JPG/390px-BEL-LUX_SO1928.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3f/BEL-LUX_SO1928.JPG 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BEL-LUX_SO1928.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hectic phase during the goal-rich Olympic win against <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_national_football_team" title="Luxembourg national football team">Luxembourg</a> in 1928 (5–3)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Football tournaments for senior men's national teams took place in six Summer Olympics between 1908 and 1936. The Belgian squad participated in all three <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the Summer Olympics">Olympic football tournaments</a> in the 1920s and kept the gold medal at home at the 1920 edition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-12"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssfOG20_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssfOG20-233">[222]</a></sup> Apart from the proper national team, two other Belgian delegations appeared at the Olympics. At the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1900_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1900 Summer Olympics">1900 Summer Olympics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1900_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_team_squads#Universit.C3.A9_de_Bruxelles" title="Football at the 1900 Summer Olympics – Men's team squads">a Belgian representation</a> with mainly students won bronze,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssfOG00_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssfOG00-234">[223]</a></sup> and at <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2008_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 2008 Summer Olympics">the 2008 edition</a>, Belgium's U-23 selection placed fourth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssfOG2008_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssfOG2008-61">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1920_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_team_squads#.C2.A0Belgium" title="Football at the 1920 Summer Olympics – Men's team squads">Belgium's 1920 Olympic squad</a> was given a <a href="/wiki/Bye_(sports)" title="Bye (sports)">bye</a> into the quarter-finals, where they won 3–1 against Spain, and reached the semi-finals, where they beat the Netherlands 3–0. In the first half of their final against Czechoslovakia, the Belgians led 2–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssfOG20_233-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssfOG20-233">[222]</a></sup> Forward Robert Coppée converted a disputed early <a href="/wiki/Penalty_kick_(association_football)" title="Penalty kick (association football)">penalty</a>, and the action in which attacker <a href="/wiki/Henri_Larnoe" title="Henri Larnoe">Henri Larnoe</a> doubled the score was also a matter of debate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISOH_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-ISOH-27">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFA1920_189-1"><a href="#cite_note-FIFA1920-189">[181]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Fouls_and_misconduct_(association_football)#Red_card_.28dismissal.29" title="Fouls and misconduct (association football)">dismissal</a> of the Czechoslovak left-back Karel Steiner, the discontented visitors left the pitch in the 40th minute. Afterwards, the away team reported their reasons for protest to the Olympic organisation;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISOH_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-ISOH-27">[24]</a></sup> these complaints were dismissed and the Czechoslovaks were disqualified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197976_28-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197976-28">[25]</a></sup> The 2–0 score was allowed to stand and Belgium were crowned the champions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197976_28-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenshaw197976-28">[25]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records_and_fixtures">Records and fixtures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Records and fixtures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team_records" title="Belgium national football team records">Belgium national football team records</a></div>
<p>As of 13 November 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the complete official match record of the Belgian national team comprises <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team_results" title="Belgium national football team results">748 games</a>: 309 wins, 160 draws and 279 losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fifa_unrec_181-1"><a href="#cite_note-fifa_unrec-181">[H]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-13"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup> During these games, the team scored 1,280 times and conceded 1,227 goals. Belgium reached its highest winning margin against <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_national_football_team" title="San Marino national football team">San Marino</a> (10–1) and <a href="/wiki/Zambia_national_football_team" title="Zambia national football team">Zambia</a> (9–0).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-14"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup> Their longest winning streak is seven wins in two periods, and their unbeaten record is fourteen consecutive official games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fifa_unrec_181-2"><a href="#cite_note-fifa_unrec-181">[H]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_25-15"><a href="#cite_note-results-25">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The entire match record can be examined on the following articles:</p>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team_results#Results_in_chronological_order" title="Belgium national football team results">Results in chronological order</a></i> lists all individual games.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team_results#Record_per_opponent" title="Belgium national football team results">Record per opponent</a></i> shows the head-to-head record against other footballing nations.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Belgium_national_football_team_managers" title="List of Belgium national football team managers">Statistics per manager</a></i> compiles an overview per managerial period.</li>
</ul>
<p>Upcoming fixtures are listed on the <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team_results_%E2%80%93_2010s#Forthcoming_fixtures" title="Belgium national football team results – 2010s">2010s results page</a>; these include the qualification matches for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_H" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group H">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Player_records">Player records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Player records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CoeckCeulemans1980_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="Player in training outfit running with the ball" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="842" data-file-width="758" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/CoeckCeulemans1980_%28cropped%29.jpg/160px-CoeckCeulemans1980_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/CoeckCeulemans1980_%28cropped%29.jpg/240px-CoeckCeulemans1980_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/CoeckCeulemans1980_%28cropped%29.jpg/320px-CoeckCeulemans1980_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CoeckCeulemans1980_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jan Ceulemans</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of 13 November 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the RBFA lists 682 players who appeared on the men's senior national team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[L]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllRedD_56-6"><a href="#cite_note-AllRedD-56">[53]</a></sup> With 96 <a href="/wiki/Cap" title="Cap">caps</a>, Jan Ceulemans featured most often;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSSSF_BelIntRec_188-1"><a href="#cite_note-RSSSF_BelIntRec-188">[180]</a></sup> he also started the most games as captain (48).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GamesPerD_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-GamesPerD-237">[225]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hector_Goetinck" title="Hector Goetinck">Hector Goetinck</a> had the longest career as an international footballer: 17 years, 6 months and 10 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllRedD_56-7"><a href="#cite_note-AllRedD-56">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bernard Voorhoof and Paul Van Himst are the highest-scoring Belgium players, with 30 goals each.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSSSF_BelIntRec_188-2"><a href="#cite_note-RSSSF_BelIntRec-188">[180]</a></sup> Those who scored the most goals in one match are Robert De Veen, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bert_De_Cleyn" title="Bert De Cleyn">Bert De Cleyn</a> and Josip Weber (5);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllRedD_56-8"><a href="#cite_note-AllRedD-56">[53]</a></sup> De Veen also holds the record for the most hat-tricks with three.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllRedD_56-9"><a href="#cite_note-AllRedD-56">[53]</a></sup> Belgium's fastest goal after the initial <a href="/wiki/Kick-off_(association_football)" title="Kick-off (association football)">kick-off</a> was scored by <a href="/wiki/Christian_Benteke" title="Christian Benteke">Christian Benteke</a>, 8.1 seconds into the match against <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_national_football_team" title="Gibraltar national football team">Gibraltar</a> on 10 October 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GamesPerD_237-1"><a href="#cite_note-GamesPerD-237">[225]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[226]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgium_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: upper-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The acronyms KBVB, URBSFA and KBFV come from the organisation's respective Dutch, French and German names: <i>Koninklijke Belgische Voetbalbond</i>, <i>Union Royale Belge des Sociétés de Football-Association</i> and <i>Königliche Belgische Fußballverband</i>.<br/>
The title of "Royal Union" was awarded on its 25th anniversary in 1920.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RBFAhist_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-RBFAhist-1">[1]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Note that this match is not considered to be a full international by the <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">English FA</a>, and does not appear in the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> team records.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">UBSFA was the acronym for the organisation's French name: <i>Union Belge des Sociétés de Football-Association</i>.<br/>
In 1920 it received the title of "Royal Union" for its 25th year of existence, and hence became the Royal Belgian Football Association.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RBFAhistFr_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-RBFAhistFr-12">[10]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-92"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-92">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Even in their last match of 1980, against Cyprus on 21 December, Belgium played in an Adidas outfit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[88]</a></sup> This suggests that Admiral's sponsorship started in 1981, contrary to what the 2014 article stated.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-93"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-93">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The timeline in the 2014 overview article stated the switch from Diadora to Nike happened in 1998. However, the 1999 article focused on this kit sponsor change which took place in mid-1999.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-158"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-158">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The interim managers were <a href="/wiki/Louis_Nicolay" title="Louis Nicolay">Louis Nicolay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franky_Vercauteren" title="Franky Vercauteren">Franky Vercauteren</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[152]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-162"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-162">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to the "<a href="/wiki/Three_points_for_a_win" title="Three points for a win">three points for a win</a>" standard</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-fifa_unrec-181"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-fifa_unrec_181-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fifa_unrec_181-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fifa_unrec_181-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Note that the friendlies against <a href="/wiki/Romania_national_football_team" title="Romania national football team">Romania</a> on 14 November 2012 and against <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_national_football_team" title="Luxembourg national football team">Luxembourg</a> on 26 May 2014 are not FIFA-recognised due to an excessive number of <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">substitutions</a> according to the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_the_Game_(association_football)" title="Laws of the Game (association football)">Laws of the Game</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FArules_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-FArules-180">[173]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-202"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-202">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Prime individual awards include being elected the season's or year's best player of a competition; prime team awards equal winning a competition. National top divisions, main national cup competitions, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> are considered.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-225"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-225">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">FIFA's initial match statistics showed 16 saves, and many news sources continue to use this number. The official FIFA statistics were updated on 5 July 2014 to show 15 saves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[215]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-229"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-229">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The other bids were from England and Italy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[218]</a></sup> whose teams did not reach the semi-finals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf72_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf72-37">[34]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-236"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-236">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Note that the RBFA does not count caps earned in the Belgian seven Summer Olympics matches, and that it does include Belgium's friendlies on 14 November 2012 and 26 May 2014 that are not FIFA-recognised due to an excessive number of substitutions according to the Laws of the Game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FArules_180-1"><a href="#cite_note-FArules-180">[173]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>
